       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The Greater Los Angeles area also has three well-known horse racing facilities:
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Anita_Park" title="Santa Anita Park">
        Santa Anita Park
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Alamitos_Race_Course" title="Los Alamitos Race Course">
        Los Alamitos Race Course
       </a>
       and the former
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Park_Racetrack" title="Hollywood Park Racetrack">
        Hollywood Park Racetrack
       </a>
       and three major motorsport venues:
       <a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Speedway" title="Auto Club Speedway">
        Auto Club Speedway
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_Beach_street_circuit" title="Long Beach street circuit">
        Long Beach street circuit
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Raceway_at_Pomona" title="Auto Club Raceway at Pomona">
        Auto Club Raceway at Pomona
       </a>
       . In addition, the city of Los Angeles hosted the Summer Olympics in
       <a href="/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics" title="1932 Summer Olympics">
        1932
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">
        1984
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       For over twenty years the Los Angeles area media market lacked a
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        National Football League
       </a>
       team. After the 1994 season, the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Los_Angeles_Rams" title="History of the Los Angeles Rams">
        Los Angeles Rams
       </a>
       moved to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">
        St. Louis, Missouri
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Los_Angeles_Raiders" title="History of the Los Angeles Raiders">
        Los Angeles Raiders
       </a>
       returned to their original home of
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland, California
       </a>
       , due to the lack of an up-to-date NFL stadium. After
       <a href="/wiki/Proposed_Los_Angeles_NFL_stadiums" title="Proposed Los Angeles NFL stadiums">
        numerous stadium proposals
       </a>
       between 1995 and 2016 in an attempt to bring the NFL back,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders" title="Oakland Raiders">
        Oakland Raiders
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis_Rams" title="St. Louis Rams">
        St. Louis Rams
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Chargers" title="San Diego Chargers">
        San Diego Chargers
       </a>
       all submitted plans to relocate back to Los Angeles after the
       <a href="/wiki/2015_NFL_season" title="2015 NFL season">
        2015 NFL season
       </a>
       . On January 12, 2016, the Rams were approved to move to Los Angeles and build
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Stadium_at_Hollywood_Park" title="Los Angeles Stadium at Hollywood Park">
        Los Angeles Stadium at Hollywood Park
       </a>
       with the Chargers or Raiders given the option to join them. On January 12, 2017, the Chargers announced their move to Los Angeles to join the Rams. The Rams temporarily play at the
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">
        Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum
       </a>
       while the Chargers temporarily play at
       <a href="/wiki/StubHub_Center" title="StubHub Center">
        StubHub Center
       </a>
       . Both teams will share the new
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Stadium_at_Hollywood_Park" title="Los Angeles Stadium at Hollywood Park">
        Los Angeles Stadium at Hollywood Park
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">
        Inglewood, California
       </a>
       , once construction is completed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-38">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation news">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.time.com/time/magazine/article/0,9171,842728-4,00.html" rel="nofollow">
            "Magnet in the West"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">
             Time
            </a>
           </i>
           . September 2, 1966
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             April 24,
            </span>
            2008
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            Greater Los Angeles is already the second-most-populous metropolis in the U.S., is almost sure to surpass New York by 1975. Last week alone, some 5,000 people moved into the area. By 1990, such growth will make the city the hub of an uninterrupted urbanized stretch of almost 19 million inhabitants occupying the 175-mile-long, coastal area that runs from Santa Barbara in the north to San Diego in the south.
           </q>
